Allah's Existence
beginner
5 min
Allah's Existence is Inherent and Uncaused
Contrasting divine and contingent existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fundamental distinction between Allah's inherent existence and the temporal, caused existence of all creatures.

Core Idea
Allah exists by Himself; everything else exists only because He brings it into being.

This lesson introduces the most basic principle of Islamic theology: the creator and the creation are not the same kind of existents. The commentary contrasts Allah's self-subsistent existence with the contingent existence of everything else, setting the stage for deeper discussions about divine attributes and the refutation of pantheistic doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and its translation
Read the source passage carefully. Notice the key contrast: 'وجود الله ذاتي' vs 'وجود الحوادث غير ذاتي'. Let the author's wording sink in.
The Arabic uses the word 'حادث' for contingent/temporal things.
2
Identify the two kinds of existence
The passage clearly distinguishes between necessary existence (Allah) and contingent existence (everything else). List the characteristics of each as mentioned.
Necessary existence: inherent, uncaused, never absent. Contingent existence: temporal, caused, accidental.
3
Reflect on the implications
If Allah's existence were not inherent, He would need a creator, leading to an infinite regress. This logical foundation supports tawhid.
This distinction is the basis for all later kalam arguments about God's attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجود الله ليس كوجود الحوادث، لأن وجود الله ذاتي له أي ليس بتأثير مؤثر وفعل فاعل، ووجود الحوادث بتأثير الله وفعله لأنه تعالى كان وحده ولا شيء غيره كما ورد في الحديث الشريف كما رواه البخاري ومسلم وغيرهما، ثم أوجد جل جلاله الحوادث، فوجودها غير ذاتي لها بل هو طارئ عليها وعارض لها، ولكون وجوده تعالى ذاتيا لم يقبل سبحانه العدم في الأزل، ولا يقبله في الأبد والأزل هو استمرار الوجود في أزمنة مقدرة غير متناهية في جانب الماضي، ويقابله الأبد وهو استمرار الوجود في أزمنة مقدرة غير متناهية في جانب المستقبل، ويعبر عنه بما لا يزال (غ) بتصرف يسير، وأما غير الله تعالى فهي موجودات لها وجود غير وجود الله تعالى، ولكنها ثابتة ومتحققة لتعلق فعل الله بها، وفعله هو تعلق قدرته، ولهذا قد يسمي البعض المخلوقات بأنها فعل الله، ولا يريد أنها مجرد تعلق أو مجرد نسبة عدمية أو إشراقية، بل يريد أن هذه المخلوقات الموجودة من متعلقات فعل الله فإذا انقطع تعلق قدرة الله تعالى ( أي فعله ) بها انعدمت المخلوقات فبقاؤها مشروط بدوام تعلق قدرة الله تعالى بها وليس فعل الله حالا بذاته وإلا لزم قيام الحوادث بذاته وغير ذلك، قال العلامة الأمير في حاشيته على شرح عبد السلام على الجوهرة: " وأما غيره - أي غير الله - فهو فعله وذهب بعض المتصوفة والفلاسفة إلى أنه تعالى الوجود المطلق، وأنَّ غيره لا يتصف بالوجود أصلاً حتى إذا قالوا: الإنسان موجود، فمعناه أنَّ له تعلقاً بالوجود وهو الله تعالى، وهو كفر، ولا حلول ولا اتحاد . اهـ وهذه كلمة شريفة منه يبين فيها فساد مذهب وحدة الوجود وأنه مخالف لعقيدة أهل السنة، ويزيد فيقول إن القائل بهذا المذهب لا يلزمه القول بالحلول والاتحاد ولذلك ترى بعض من يقول بوحدة الوجود ينفي الحلول والاتحاد مخادعاً للناس لأن كثيرا منهم يظن أن مذهب وحدة الوجود يلزمه القول بالحلول والاتحاد فهو يكتفي بنفي الحلول والاتحاد ليوهمهم أنه لا يخالف مذهب أهل السنة ومن ينخدع به لا يعرف ما ذكرناه، بل مذهب وحدة الوجود مبني على نفي تكثر الوجود وأما القول بالحلول والاتحاد فهما مبنيَّان على القول بتكثر الوجود، وإلا فلا حلول ولا اتحاد فتأمل. فيما ذكرناه هنا فهو مفيد جداً.
The existence of Allah is not like the existence of contingent things, because the existence of Allah is inherent to Him, meaning it is not by the influence of an influencer or the act of an agent. The existence of contingent things is through the influence and act of Allah, because He, exalted, was alone and nothing else with Him, as reported in the noble hadith narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and others. Then He, majestic is His glory, brought contingent things into existence, so their existence is not inherent to them, but rather it is temporal and accidental to them. Because His existence, exalted, is inherent, He, glorified, did not accept non-existence in pre-eternity (azal), nor does He accept it in post-eternity (abad). Azal is the continuation of existence in hypothetical times that are infinite in the past direction, and its opposite is abad, which is the continuation of existence in hypothetical times infinite in the future direction, and it is expressed as 'what continues without end' (ma la yazal) with slight modification. As for other than Allah, exalted, they are existents that have an existence different from the existence of Allah, exalted, but they are fixed and realized due to the attachment of Allah's act to them, and His act is the attachment of His power. For this reason, some may call creatures 'the act of Allah', not meaning that they are mere attachment or a non-existent or emanative relationship, but rather they mean that these existing creatures are among the attachments of Allah's act. When the attachment of Allah's power (i.e., His act) to them is cut off, the creatures become non-existent, so their continuance is conditioned by the continuance of the attachment of Allah's power to them. And Allah's act is not a state inherent in His essence, otherwise the occurrence of temporal events in His essence would follow, etc. Al-‘Allama al-Amir said in his gloss on the commentary of ‘Abd al-Salam on al-Jawhara: 'As for other than Him – i.e., other than Allah – it is His act. And some Sufis and philosophers held that He, exalted, is absolute existence, and that other than Him is not described by existence at all, so that when they say 'man exists', its meaning is that he has an attachment to existence, which is Allah, exalted. This is unbelief. There is neither indwelling (hulul) nor union (ittihad).' End quote. This is a noble statement from him in which he shows the corruption of the doctrine of unity of existence (wahdat al-wujud) and that it contradicts the creed of Ahl al-Sunna. He adds, saying: The proponent of this doctrine is not necessarily led to say indwelling or union, so you see some who say unity of existence denying indwelling and union, deceiving people, because many of them think that the doctrine of unity of existence necessarily requires saying indwelling and union. So he is satisfied with denying indwelling and union to make them believe that he does not contradict the school of Ahl al-Sunna. Whoever is deceived by him does not know what we have mentioned. Rather, the doctrine of unity of existence is based on negating multiplicity of existence, while the claim of indwelling and union are based on affirming multiplicity of existence. Otherwise, there is no indwelling or union. So ponder. What we have mentioned here is very beneficial.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the nature of divine existence and refuting the doctrine of wahdat al-wujud (unity of existence). It begins by contrasting the existence of Allah with that of contingent things: Allah's existence is inherent (dhati) and uncaused, while creatures' existence is temporal and caused by Allah's act. It defines azal (pre-eternity) as infinite past and abad (post-eternity) as infinite future. Creatures depend on the continuous attachment of Allah's power for their existence. The commentary then quotes al-Amir to refute wahdat al-wujud, which holds that only Allah truly exists and creatures are mere attachments; this is declared kufr. The passage clarifies that wahdat al-wujud does not entail hulul (indwelling) or ittihad (union), as it negates multiplicity, while hulul and ittihad presuppose multiple existents. The deception of those who deny hulul and ittihad while holding wahdat al-wujud is exposed.

Key Terms
وجود ذاتي
حادث
عارض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is Allah's existence different from the existence of creatures?
A) Because Allah's existence is inherent, while creatures' existence is caused by Him.
B) Because Allah's existence is eternal, but creatures can also be eternal.
C) Because Allah's existence is temporal, while creatures are inherent.
D) Because there is no real difference; all existence is the same.

Key Takeaway
Allah's existence is self-subsistent and uncaused; all other existence is temporary and dependent on Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your very existence at this moment depends entirely on Allah sustaining you, what does that say about your self-reliance? Where in your life do you behave as if you are the one in control, and how can you surrender that illusion right now?
?
When you read that Allah 'was alone, nothing with Him' and then created you, do you feel the weight of being called into being by His sheer will? What does that imply about the purpose He placed in you? Are you living that purpose or ignoring it?
?
Allah's existence is inherent—He needs nothing. Your existence is accidental—you need Him at every breath. If you truly internalized this, would you still hold grudges, fear people, or chase status? What is the one thing you can do today to let this truth reshape your heart?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
6 min
Azal, Abad, and the Dependence of Creatures
Defining azal/abad and explaining creaturely dependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concepts of azal and abad and why creatures continuously depend on Allah's power for their continued existence.

Core Idea
Only Allah is eternal; creatures hang on His power every moment.

After establishing that Allah's existence is inherent, the commentary now defines the terms 'azal' (pre-eternity) and 'abad' (post-eternity). It also explains that creatures do not become self-sufficient once created; they need the continuous attachment of Allah's power to remain in existence. This lesson deepens our understanding of tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the definitions of azal and abad
The passage defines azal as infinite past and abad as infinite future. Compare these to the English terms 'pre-eternity' and 'post-eternity'. Note that these are hypothetical times.
Azal is not a time period; it is the conceptual infinite past.
2
Understand the dependence of creatures
The passage states that creatures exist due to the attachment of Allah's power. If that attachment ceases, they become non-existent. This is a key Ash'ari doctrine of continuous creation.
This is different from the idea that God created once and then left things to run on their own.
3
Reflect on the contrast
Allah's existence is not subject to time; creatures depend on the time of Allah's act. Allah is eternal in both directions; creatures are temporal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجود الله ليس كوجود الحوادث، لأن وجود الله ذاتي له أي ليس بتأثير مؤثر وفعل فاعل، ووجود الحوادث بتأثير الله وفعله لأنه تعالى كان وحده ولا شيء غيره كما ورد في الحديث الشريف كما رواه البخاري ومسلم وغيرهما، ثم أوجد جل جلاله الحوادث، فوجودها غير ذاتي لها بل هو طارئ عليها وعارض لها، ولكون وجوده تعالى ذاتيا لم يقبل سبحانه العدم في الأزل، ولا يقبله في الأبد والأزل هو استمرار الوجود في أزمنة مقدرة غير متناهية في جانب الماضي، ويقابله الأبد وهو استمرار الوجود في أزمنة مقدرة غير متناهية في جانب المستقبل، ويعبر عنه بما لا يزال (غ) بتصرف يسير، وأما غير الله تعالى فهي موجودات لها وجود غير وجود الله تعالى، ولكنها ثابتة ومتحققة لتعلق فعل الله بها، وفعله هو تعلق قدرته، ولهذا قد يسمي البعض المخلوقات بأنها فعل الله، ولا يريد أنها مجرد تعلق أو مجرد نسبة عدمية أو إشراقية، بل يريد أن هذه المخلوقات الموجودة من متعلقات فعل الله فإذا انقطع تعلق قدرة الله تعالى ( أي فعله ) بها انعدمت المخلوقات فبقاؤها مشروط بدوام تعلق قدرة الله تعالى بها وليس فعل الله حالا بذاته وإلا لزم قيام الحوادث بذاته وغير ذلك، قال العلامة الأمير في حاشيته على شرح عبد السلام على الجوهرة: " وأما غيره - أي غير الله - فهو فعله وذهب بعض المتصوفة والفلاسفة إلى أنه تعالى الوجود المطلق، وأنَّ غيره لا يتصف بالوجود أصلاً حتى إذا قالوا: الإنسان موجود، فمعناه أنَّ له تعلقاً بالوجود وهو الله تعالى، وهو كفر، ولا حلول ولا اتحاد . اهـ وهذه كلمة شريفة منه يبين فيها فساد مذهب وحدة الوجود وأنه مخالف لعقيدة أهل السنة، ويزيد فيقول إن القائل بهذا المذهب لا يلزمه القول بالحلول والاتحاد ولذلك ترى بعض من يقول بوحدة الوجود ينفي الحلول والاتحاد مخادعاً للناس لأن كثيرا منهم يظن أن مذهب وحدة الوجود يلزمه القول بالحلول والاتحاد فهو يكتفي بنفي الحلول والاتحاد ليوهمهم أنه لا يخالف مذهب أهل السنة ومن ينخدع به لا يعرف ما ذكرناه، بل مذهب وحدة الوجود مبني على نفي تكثر الوجود وأما القول بالحلول والاتحاد فهما مبنيَّان على القول بتكثر الوجود، وإلا فلا حلول ولا اتحاد فتأمل. فيما ذكرناه هنا فهو مفيد جداً.
The existence of Allah is not like the existence of contingent things, because the existence of Allah is inherent to Him, meaning it is not by the influence of an influencer or the act of an agent. The existence of contingent things is through the influence and act of Allah, because He, exalted, was alone and nothing else with Him, as reported in the noble hadith narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and others. Then He, majestic is His glory, brought contingent things into existence, so their existence is not inherent to them, but rather it is temporal and accidental to them. Because His existence, exalted, is inherent, He, glorified, did not accept non-existence in pre-eternity (azal), nor does He accept it in post-eternity (abad). Azal is the continuation of existence in hypothetical times that are infinite in the past direction, and its opposite is abad, which is the continuation of existence in hypothetical times infinite in the future direction, and it is expressed as 'what continues without end' (ma la yazal) with slight modification. As for other than Allah, exalted, they are existents that have an existence different from the existence of Allah, exalted, but they are fixed and realized due to the attachment of Allah's act to them, and His act is the attachment of His power. For this reason, some may call creatures 'the act of Allah', not meaning that they are mere attachment or a non-existent or emanative relationship, but rather they mean that these existing creatures are among the attachments of Allah's act. When the attachment of Allah's power (i.e., His act) to them is cut off, the creatures become non-existent, so their continuance is conditioned by the continuance of the attachment of Allah's power to them. And Allah's act is not a state inherent in His essence, otherwise the occurrence of temporal events in His essence would follow, etc. Al-‘Allama al-Amir said in his gloss on the commentary of ‘Abd al-Salam on al-Jawhara: 'As for other than Him – i.e., other than Allah – it is His act. And some Sufis and philosophers held that He, exalted, is absolute existence, and that other than Him is not described by existence at all, so that when they say 'man exists', its meaning is that he has an attachment to existence, which is Allah, exalted. This is unbelief. There is neither indwelling (hulul) nor union (ittihad).' End quote. This is a noble statement from him in which he shows the corruption of the doctrine of unity of existence (wahdat al-wujud) and that it contradicts the creed of Ahl al-Sunna. He adds, saying: The proponent of this doctrine is not necessarily led to say indwelling or union, so you see some who say unity of existence denying indwelling and union, deceiving people, because many of them think that the doctrine of unity of existence necessarily requires saying indwelling and union. Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the nature of divine existence and refuting the doctrine of wahdat al-wujud (unity of existence). It begins by contrasting the existence of Allah with that of contingent things: Allah's existence is inherent (dhati) and uncaused, while creatures' existence is temporal and caused by Allah's act. It defines azal (pre-eternity) as infinite past and abad (post-eternity) as infinite future. Creatures depend on the continuous attachment of Allah's power for their existence. The commentary then quotes al-Amir to refute wahdat al-wujud, which holds that only Allah truly exists and creatures are mere attachments; this is declared kufr. The passage clarifies that wahdat al-wujud does not entail hulul (indwelling) or ittihad (union), as it negates multiplicity, while hulul and ittihad presuppose multiple existents. The deception of those who deny hulul and ittihad while holding wahdat al-wujud is exposed.

Key Terms
أزل
أبد
تعلق القدرة
فعل الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must be met for creatures to continue existing?
A) They must maintain their own essence.
B) The continuous attachment of Allah's power to them.
C) They must exist in their own right.
D) They must be eternal like Allah.

Key Takeaway
Everything other than Allah exists only as long as Allah's power continuously sustains it; nothing is self-sufficient.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that creatures are only sustained by Allah's continuous power. But do you truly feel this dependency in your daily life? Or do you wake up feeling self-sufficient, forgetting that at any moment Allah could withdraw His sustaining act? How would your morning du'a change if you truly believed that every breath is a new act of attachment from Him? Will you pause right now and say 'Alhamdulillah' for each limb that still functions, acknowledging that only Allah keeps them existing?
?
The passage defines azal as Allah's infinite past. You did not exist in that azal. Your existence began at a specific moment, and it continues only because Allah’s power is still attached to you. Knowing that your entire being is a continuous gift, what plans have you made today that assume you will live until tomorrow? Are you arrogantly planning a future as if you own it? How will you surrender your plans to Allah right now, recognizing that without His constant act, you are nothing?
?
Consider the people and things you love most: your family, your health, your possessions. The lesson says they would become non-existent if Allah cut off His power attachment. Have you ever thanked Allah for keeping them in existence this very moment? Or do you take them for granted? Can you, right now, in your heart, make a silent commitment to recite Surah al-Ikhlas and reflect that only Allah is independent, while everything else is dependent on Him?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
7 min
Refuting Wahdat al-Wujud and Clarifying Hulul and Ittihad
Refuting wahdat al-wujud and explaining its relation to hulul/ittihad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the doctrine of wahdat al-wujud is considered kufr and why it does not necessarily entail hulul or ittihad.

Core Idea
Wahdat al-wujud denies that creatures truly exist, which contradicts tawhid and the reality of creation.

This lesson tackles a dangerous deviation: the claim that only Allah truly exists and that creatures are mere illusions or attachments of the divine. The commentary exposes the falsity of this view and shows how some proponents deceive others by denying hulul and ittihad while still holding to wahdat al-wujud. Understanding this helps protect the creed of Ahl al-Sunna.

Guided Path
1
Read the quoted statement from al-Amir
Al-Amir declares that the doctrine that only Allah exists and creatures are mere attachments is kufr. He also says there is no hulul or ittihad in this view.
Note that he says 'لا حلول ولا اتحاد' – meaning the proponents themselves reject these ideas.
2
Understand the basis of the refutation
The author explains that wahdat al-wujud is based on negating multiplicity of existence, while hulul and ittihad assume multiplicity. So those who hold wahdat al-wujud can consistently deny hulul/ittihad, but this is a deception.
People mistakenly think that if someone denies hulul/ittihad, he must not be a follower of wahdat al-wujud.
3
Reflect on the deception
The author warns that such denials are a trick to appear orthodox. The real issue is that wahdat al-wujud itself is kufr, regardless of whether it includes hulul/ittihad.
This is a key point in sectarian discussions.

Source Text

وجود الله ليس كوجود الحوادث، لأن وجود الله ذاتي له أي ليس بتأثير مؤثر وفعل فاعل، ووجود الحوادث بتأثير الله وفعله لأنه تعالى كان وحده ولا شيء غيره كما ورد في الحديث الشريف كما رواه البخاري ومسلم وغيرهما، ثم أوجد جل جلاله الحوادث، فوجودها غير ذاتي لها بل هو طارئ عليها وعارض لها، ولكون وجوده تعالى ذاتيا لم يقبل سبحانه العدم في الأزل، ولا يقبله في الأبد والأزل هو استمرار الوجود في أزمنة مقدرة غير متناهية في جانب الماضي، ويقابله الأبد وهو استمرار الوجود في أزمنة مقدرة غير متناهية في جانب المستقبل، ويعبر عنه بما لا يزال (غ) بتصرف يسير، وأما غير الله تعالى فهي موجودات لها وجود غير وجود الله تعالى، ولكنها ثابتة ومتحققة لتعلق فعل الله بها، وفعله هو تعلق قدرته، ولهذا قد يسمي البعض المخلوقات بأنها فعل الله، ولا يريد أنها مجرد تعلق أو مجرد نسبة عدمية أو إشراقية، بل يريد أن هذه المخلوقات الموجودة من متعلقات فعل الله فإذا انقطع تعلق قدرة الله تعالى ( أي فعله ) بها انعدمت المخلوقات فبقاؤها مشروط بدوام تعلق قدرة الله تعالى بها وليس فعل الله حالا بذاته وإلا لزم قيام الحوادث بذاته وغير ذلك، قال العلامة الأمير في حاشيته على شرح عبد السلام على الجوهرة: " وأما غيره - أي غير الله - فهو فعله وذهب بعض المتصوفة والفلاسفة إلى أنه تعالى الوجود المطلق، وأنَّ غيره لا يتصف بالوجود أصلاً حتى إذا قالوا: الإنسان موجود، فمعناه أنَّ له تعلقاً بالوجود وهو الله تعالى، وهو كفر، ولا حلول ولا اتحاد . اهـ وهذه كلمة شريفة منه يبين فيها فساد مذهب وحدة الوجود وأنه مخالف لعقيدة أهل السنة، ويزيد فيقول إن القائل بهذا المذهب لا يلزمه القول بالحلول والاتحاد ولذلك ترى بعض من يقول بوحدة الوجود ينفي الحلول والاتحاد مخادعاً للناس لأن كثيرا منهم يظن أن مذهب وحدة الوجود يلزمه القول بالحلول والاتحاد فهو يكتفي بنفي الحلول والاتحاد ليوهمهم أنه لا يخالف مذهب أهل السنة ومن ينخدع به لا يعرف ما ذكرناه، بل مذهب وحدة الوجود مبني على نفي تكثر الوجود وأما القول بالحلول والاتحاد فهما مبنيَّان على القول بتكثر الوجود، وإلا فلا حلول ولا اتحاد فتأمل. فيما ذكرناه هنا فهو مفيد جداً.
The existence of Allah is not like the existence of contingent things, because the existence of Allah is inherent to Him, meaning it is not by the influence of an influencer or the act of an agent. The existence of contingent things is through the influence and act of Allah, because He, exalted, was alone and nothing else with Him, as reported in the noble hadith narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and others. Then He, majestic is His glory, brought contingent things into existence, so their existence is not inherent to them, but rather it is temporal and accidental to them. Because His existence, exalted, is inherent, He, glorified, did not accept non-existence in pre-eternity (azal), nor does He accept it in post-eternity (abad). Azal is the continuation of existence in hypothetical times that are infinite in the past direction, and its opposite is abad, which is the continuation of existence in hypothetical times infinite in the future direction, and it is expressed as 'what continues without end' (ma la yazal) with slight modification. As for other than Allah, exalted, they are existents that have an existence different from the existence of Allah, exalted, but they are fixed and realized due to the attachment of Allah's act to them, and His act is the attachment of His power. For this reason, some may call creatures 'the act of Allah', not meaning that they are mere attachment or a non-existent or emanative relationship, but rather they mean that these existing creatures are among the attachments of Allah's act. When the attachment of Allah's power (i.e., His act) to them is cut off, the creatures become non-existent, so their continuance is conditioned by the continuance of the attachment of Allah's power to them. And Allah's act is not a state inherent in His essence, otherwise the occurrence of temporal events in His essence would follow, etc. Al-‘Allama al-Amir said in his gloss on the commentary of ‘Abd al-Salam on al-Jawhara: 'As for other than Him – i.e., other than Allah – it is His act. And some Sufis and philosophers held that He, exalted, is absolute existence, and that other than Him is not described by existence at all, so that when they say 'man exists', its meaning is that he has an attachment to existence, which is Allah, exalted. This is unbelief. There is neither indwelling (hulul) nor union (ittihad).' End quote. This is a noble statement from him in which he shows the corruption of the doctrine of unity of existence (wahdat al-wujud) and that it contradicts the creed of Ahl al-Sunna. He adds, saying: The proponent of this doctrine is not necessarily led to say indwelling or union, so you see some who say unity of existence denying indwelling and union, deceiving people, because many of them think that the doctrine of unity of existence necessarily requires saying indwelling and union. So he is satisfied with denying indwelling and union to make them believe that he does not contradict the school of Ahl al-Sunna. Whoever is deceived by him does not know what we have mentioned. Rather, the doctrine of unity of existence is based on negating multiplicity of existence, while the claim of indwelling and union are based on affirming multiplicity of existence. Otherwise, there is no indwelling or union. So ponder. What we have mentioned here is very beneficial.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the nature of divine existence and refuting the doctrine of wahdat al-wujud (unity of existence). It begins by contrasting the existence of Allah with that of contingent things: Allah's existence is inherent (dhati) and uncaused, while creatures' existence is temporal and caused by Allah's act. It defines azal (pre-eternity) as infinite past and abad (post-eternity) as infinite future. Creatures depend on the continuous attachment of Allah's power for their existence. The commentary then quotes al-Amir to refute wahdat al-wujud, which holds that only Allah truly exists and creatures are mere attachments; this is declared kufr. The passage clarifies that wahdat al-wujud does not entail hulul (indwelling) or ittihad (union), as it negates multiplicity, while hulul and ittihad presuppose multiple existents. The deception of those who deny hulul and ittihad while holding wahdat al-wujud is exposed.

Key Terms
وحدة الوجود
حلول
اتحاد
تكاثر الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume that wahdat al-wujud necessarily implies hulul or ittihad, and that denying these means rejecting wahdat al-wujud.
Correction: The passage explains that wahdat al-wujud is based on negating multiplicity, so it does not lead to hulul/ittihad. But the doctrine itself is still kufr. Denying hulul/ittihad does not mean the person rejects wahdat al-wujud.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do some proponents of wahdat al-wujud deny hulul and ittihad?
A) Because they truly believe in the separation of God and creation.
B) To deceive people into thinking they follow Ahl al-Sunna.
C) Because they think hulul and ittihad are heresies.
D) Because they misunderstand their own doctrine.

Key Takeaway
Wahdat al-wujud is kufr regardless of whether it denies hulul/ittihad; it denies the real existence of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt impressed by someone who denies hulul and ittihad, thinking they are defending tawhid, without realizing they might actually be promoting wahdat al-wujud? Examine your heart: are you more concerned with appearing open-minded than with holding firm to the truth that creation is real and distinct from Allah?
?
When you say 'Allahu Akbar,' do you truly affirm that Allah is greater than anything in existence, yet also affirm that your own existence is not an illusion? Or do you secretly harbor a sense that only Allah exists and you are just a wave in the ocean of His being? This lesson demands that you choose: will you repent from any trace of wahdat al-wujud in your heart?
?
Suppose a friend tells you that 'everything is God' to comfort someone. How would you respond using the distinction in this passage? But first, ask yourself: is there any part of you that finds that idea comforting because it avoids the hard truth that you are a dependent creature with real choices and accountability?

The Three Aspects of Divine Oneness
Sanusi defines wahdaniyya as negation of multiplicity in three domains with two types each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three domains of divine oneness (essence, attributes, actions) and how each negates two types of multiplicity.

Core Idea
Divine oneness means no multiplicity in essence, attributes, or actions — inside or outside.

Sanusi now defines wahdaniyya, the oneness of Allah, as the negation of multiplicity. He unpacks this into three domains: essence, attributes, and actions. For each domain, he explains what is meant by negation of internal (connected) and external (separate) multiplicity. This passage is foundational for understanding Islamic monotheism.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the repetition of 'connected and separate quantity' for each domain.
2
Identify the three domains
The passage divides oneness into essence, attributes, and actions. Find where each is introduced.
Look for the phrases 'وحدانية الذات', 'وحدانية الصفات', 'وحدانية الأفعال'.
3
Examine each type of negation
For each domain, note what 'connected quantity' and 'separate quantity' negate. Write down the specific examples.
Connected = internal multiplicity; separate = external equal or partner.
4
Understand the argument for essence
Sanusi argues that composition (connected) would imply contingency. Why? Because every composite depends on its parts.
Apply the principle of need: what is composed needs its components.
5
Reflect on the overall tawhid picture
Consider how these three negations together establish Allah's absolute uniqueness. No one shares His essence, attributes, or actions.
Tawhid is not just a statement; it has specific content that refutes shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامسة: الوحدانية): وحقيقة الوحدانية عبارة عن نفي التعدد في الذات والصفات والأفعال فهو سبحانه لا شبيه له في ذاته ولا في صفاته ولا في أفعاله فوحدانية الذات تنفي الكم المتصل والمنفصل ؛ فالمتصل أن تكون ذاته مركبة (۳) من جواهر وأعراض أو أن تكون مركبة مطلقاً ولو من غير الجوهر والعرض كالهيولى والصورة أو أي أمر آخر مفترض والتركب على الله تعالى محال، لأنه لو كان مركبا لكان حادثا للزوم احتياج كل مركب ؛ والمنفصل أن تكون ذات أخرى يجب لها من الكمال ما يجب الله ويستحيل عليها من النقص ما يستحيل عليه، وهذا محال لأن الله لا شريك له ولا نظير. ووحدانية الصفات تنفي الكم المتصل والمنفصل فالمتصل أن يكون له قدرتان وإرادتان وهكذا إلى آخر الصفات، بل قدرته واحدة وإرادته واحدة وعلمه واحد وهكذا. والمنفصل أن يكون لغيره صفة كمال مثل صفاته، بل صفاته لا يشبهه فيها أحد. ووحدانية الأفعال تنفي الكم المتصل والمنفصل فالمتصل أن يكون له فعلان فصاعداً من جنس واحد في محل واحد في زمان واحد، والمنفصل أن يكون لغيره فعل اختياري كفعله أو تأثير فيه، بل لا فاعل على الحقيقة إلا الله (١). (س).
The fifth [section]: al-Wahdaniyya (Oneness). The reality of wahdaniyya is the negation of multiplicity in the essence, attributes, and actions. So He, exalted, has no likeness in His essence, nor in His attributes, nor in His actions. The oneness of essence negates connected and separate quantity. Connected [quantity] is that His essence be composed of atoms and accidents, or that it be composed absolutely, even if not of atom and accident, like matter and form or any other supposed thing. Composition with respect to Allah is impossible, because if He were composed, He would be contingent due to the necessity of every composite being in need. Separate [quantity] is that there be another essence for which is necessary the same perfection that is necessary for Allah and impossible the same deficiency that is impossible for Him. This is impossible because Allah has no partner and no equal. The oneness of attributes negates connected and separate quantity. Connected is that He have two powers, two wills, and so on to the end of the attributes; rather, His power is one, His will is one, His knowledge is one, and so on. Separate is that another have an attribute of perfection like His attributes; rather, no one resembles Him in His attributes. The oneness of actions negates connected and separate quantity. Connected is that He have two or more actions of the same kind in one locus at one time. Separate is that another have an independent voluntary action like His action or an effect in it; rather, there is no true agent except Allah. (S).
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage defines al-wahdaniyya (oneness) as the negation of multiplicity in three domains: essence, attributes, and actions. For each, it explains what is negated under two types of quantity (kamm): connected (muttasil) and separate (munfasil). Connected quantity refers to internal multiplicity or composition; separate quantity refers to external multiplicity or another equal. For essence: connected composition (e.g., being made of parts) is impossible because it would entail contingency; separate essence (another god) is impossible because Allah has no partner. For attributes: connected multiplicity (e.g., two powers) is denied; attributes are singular. Separate multiplicity (another having the same perfect attribute) is denied; no one shares Allah's attributes. For actions: connected multiplicity (two same actions in one place and time) is denied; separate action (another true agent) is denied; only Allah is the true agent. This is the standard Ash'ari doctrine of tawhid.

Key Terms
الوحدانية
نفي التعدد
الكم المتصل
الكم المنفصل
الذات
الصفات
الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'oneness of attributes' means Allah has only one attribute (e.g., existence) rather than many.
Correction: It means each attribute is singular and unique; there are multiple attributes (power, will, knowledge), but no multiplicity within a given attribute (no two powers).

Checkpoint
What does wahdaniyya of actions negate regarding external agents?
A) That Allah cannot create
B) That another can act independently like Allah
C) That actions are eternal
D) That humans have no free will

Key Takeaway
Divine oneness means that Allah is unique in His essence, attributes, and actions, and nothing shares in these.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you realise that 'there is no true agent except Allah', what does that mean for how you approach your own actions and choices? Are there areas where you act as if you are the ultimate cause?
?
Do you ever find yourself attributing perfect qualities to people or things in your life (like intelligence, power, or beauty) in a way that rivals how you see Allah? How does the negation of separate quantity in attributes challenge this?
?
If Allah is absolutely unique in His essence, what does that demand from you when you are tempted to compare Him to anything or to feel that something else holds ultimate significance? How can you actively guard your heart against this?

Divine Unity and Unity of Essence
Sanusi defines divine unity and explains unity of essence with its two negations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of divine unity as the negation of multiplicity in God's essence, attributes, and acts, and how unity of essence negates both continuous and discrete composition.

Core Idea
Divine unity means negating all multiplicity in essence, attributes, and acts — not just believing in one God.

Sanusi begins the fifth section by defining the reality of divine unity. He explains that it is not a simple affirmation of oneness but a comprehensive negation of any multiplicity in God's essence, attributes, and acts. He then focuses on unity of essence and explains the two types of composition it negates.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the full translation. Notice how Sanusi defines unity and then breaks it down into types.
Pay attention to the two categories: continuous and discrete quantity.
2
Identify the definition of divine unity
Find the sentence that defines unity as 'negation of multiplicity' in essence, attributes, and acts. Understand that this is the core meaning.
This definition frames the entire discussion.
3
Understand the two negations of unity of essence
The passage explains that unity of essence negates continuous quantity (composition) and discrete quantity (another equal essence). Study each one with its examples.
Continuous composition includes substances and accidents; discrete means a second god.
4
Reflect on the logical proof
Sanusi argues that composition would entail contingency (need for parts), which is impossible for God. Consider why this is a necessary implication.
This connects to broader kalam proofs for God's oneness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامسة: الوحدانية): وحقيقة الوحدانية عبارة عن نفي التعدد في الذات والصفات والأفعال فهو سبحانه لا شبيه له في ذاته ولا في صفاته ولا في أفعاله فوحدانية الذات تنفي الكم المتصل والمنفصل ؛ فالمتصل أن تكون ذاته مركبة (۳) من جواهر وأعراض أو أن تكون مركبة مطلقاً ولو من غير الجوهر والعرض كالهيولى والصورة أو أي أمر آخر مفترض والتركب على الله تعالى محال، لأنه لو كان مركبا لكان حادثا للزوم احتياج كل مركب ؛ والمنفصل أن تكون ذات أخرى يجب لها من الكمال ما يجب الله ويستحيل عليها من النقص ما يستحيل عليه، وهذا محال لأن الله لا شريك له ولا نظير.
The fifth [section]: Unity (al-wahdaniyyah): And the reality of unity is an expression of negating multiplicity in the Essence, Attributes, and Acts. So He, glorified, has no likeness in His Essence, nor in His Attributes, nor in His Acts. So unity of Essence negates continuous and discrete quantity. As for continuous [quantity], it is that His Essence be composed (3) of substances and accidents, or that it be composed absolutely, even if not from substance and accident, like matter and form or any other supposed thing; and composition in respect to Allah, exalted, is impossible, because if He were composed He would be originated, due to the necessity of every composite being in need [of its parts]. As for discrete [quantity], it is that there be another essence for which is obligatory the perfection that is obligatory for Allah and for which is impossible the deficiency that is impossible for Him; and this is impossible because Allah has no partner and no equal.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation. It begins by stating that the fifth section is on divine unity (al-wahdaniyyah). It then defines the reality of unity as the negation of multiplicity in God's Essence, Attributes, and Acts. The author then focuses on unity of Essence, stating that it negates two types of quantity: continuous and discrete. Continuous quantity is negated by denying any composition in God's Essence, whether from substances and accidents or any other components; such composition would entail origination because every composite requires its parts. Discrete quantity is negated by denying the existence of another essence that shares the same perfections and lacks the same imperfections as God; this would imply a partner or equal, which is impossible.

Key Terms
الوحدانية
الذات
الكم المتصل
الكم المنفصل
التركب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that divine unity simply means 'God is one' without understanding it as a negation of all multiplicity in essence, attributes, and acts.
Correction: The passage shows that unity is specifically defined as negating multiplicity in three domains: essence, attributes, and acts. For the essence, it negates both internal composition (continuous) and external equality (discrete).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'unity of essence' (وحدانية الذات) negate?
A) Only the possibility of God having parts
B) Both continuous and discrete multiplicity
C) Only discrete multiplicity
D) Only the existence of other gods

Key Takeaway
Divine unity fundamentally negates all multiplicity in God's essence, attributes, and acts, and unity of essence specifically negates any composition or equal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you contemplate Allah's oneness, do you only think 'there is no god but Allah,' or have you ever considered that His Essence cannot be composed of any parts? How does this truth affect your awe of Him? Will you take a moment today to consciously negate any mental image of Allah having parts or being like anything?
?
This lesson teaches that unity of Essence negates any equal in perfection. Is there anyone or anything in your life to whom you attribute the same ultimate authority or reliance that belongs only to Allah? How can you actively uproot that hidden association today?
?
The argument says composition implies need and thus origination. Do you live as though Allah is completely self-sufficient and needless, or do you sometimes act as if He needs your worship? What specific action will you take tomorrow to affirm His self-sufficiency in your heart and deeds?

Unity of Divine Acts: Negating Partners in Creation
Sanusi defines unity of acts and negates partners in creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what is meant by unity of divine acts and why creatures have no real causal power.

Core Idea
Only Allah creates; creatures merely acquire actions.

We have already seen that Allah is one in essence and attributes. Now Sanusi turns to the unity of His acts. This principle clarifies that no other being can create or annihilate as Allah does. Creatures do perform actions, but these actions are created by Allah and only 'acquired' by them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the key terms like 'وحدانية الأفعال' and 'الكسب'. Let the text's own wording settle in before analysis.
Pay attention to the phrase 'ينفي الكم المنفصل فقط'.
2
Identify what is negated
The passage states that unity of acts negates only 'discrete quantity' (الكم المنفصل). This means it denies that any other being can perform acts in the same manner as Allah. Recognize that this is different from unity of essence and attributes.
Discrete quantity here refers to multiple agents capable of creating independently.
3
Understand the role of creatures
Creatures have no effective power; they only 'acquire' (الكسب) actions that Allah creates in them. Grasp that all acts belong to Allah, and creatures are merely the locus of occurrence. This is a key Ash'ari doctrine.
Acquisition means the act occurs in the creature but is created by Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووحدانية الأفعال تنفي الكم المنفصل فقط، بأن يكون غيره يفعل كفعله وهذا محال ، لأن الله لا شريك له في أفعاله بل هو المنفرد بالإيجاد والإعدام ، والمخلوقات ليس لها تأثير إلا قيام الفعل بها نتيجة لاكتسابها له، ويجب أن نعتقد أن الأفعال كلها لله تعالى (۳)
And unity of Acts negates discrete quantity only, in that other than Him acts like His act; and this is impossible, because Allah has no partner in His acts. Rather, He alone brings into existence and annihilates, and creatures have no effect except the occurrence of the act in them as a result of their acquisition of it. And it is necessary to believe that all acts belong to Allah, exalted (3).
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage explains the unity of divine acts. Unlike the previous two unities, unity of acts negates only discrete quantity — meaning that no other being performs acts like God's acts. God has no partner in His acts; He alone creates and annihilates. Creatures have no independent causal effect; they only 'acquire' (kash) the act, meaning the act occurs in them but is created by God. The passage emphasizes the necessity of believing that all acts are ultimately from God.

Key Terms
وحدانية الأفعال
الإيجاد
الإعدام
الكسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that creatures create their own actions independently, like a person truly creating their own hand movement.
Correction: The passage clarifies that creatures have no effect; they merely acquire actions that Allah creates. The act occurs in them, but Allah is the sole creator.

Checkpoint
How does unity of acts differ from unity of essence and attributes in terms of the type of quantity it negates?
A) It negates both continuous and discrete quantity
B) It negates only continuous quantity
C) It negates only discrete quantity
D) It negates neither

Key Takeaway
Unity of acts means that only Allah creates and annihilates; creatures merely acquire actions that Allah creates in them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed at something, do you truly feel in your heart that Allah alone created that success, or does a secret sense of self-achievement linger? How can you train your inner state to constantly attribute every outcome to Him alone?
?
If all acts belong to Allah, what then is the real source of your worry or pride? Will you commit today to repeating 'Allah alone creates' whenever you catch yourself taking credit or fearing failure?
?
Your 'acquisition' of actions means you are responsible, yet Allah is the sole creator. Does this humble you or unsettle you? How will you live out this balance in your next decision?

Oneness of God’s Attributes and Negation of Likeness
Sanusi explains oneness of attributes and negates likeness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God's attributes are each single in essence yet relate to all possible things, making multiplicity impossible, and why no creature can possess attributes like God's.

Core Idea
God's attributes are one in essence; creatures cannot share His perfections.

Sanusi begins by clarifying a common confusion: if God has many attributes, does that make Him multiple? He explains that each attribute is inherently one, yet relates to all its objects without division. He then denies that any creature can have attributes similar to God's, because God has no likeness. This lesson lays the foundation for understanding tawhid in attributes.

Guided Path
1
Understand the oneness of each attribute
Read the first part of the passage where Sanusi states that God's power, knowledge, and will are each one in essence but relate to all their respective objects. Notice that this prevents multiplicity in the divine essence.
The attributes are not many separate entities; each is a single perfection.
2
See why multiplicity is impossible
Reflect on the statement 'multiplicity in attributes is impossible.' Understand that if each attribute were multiple, it would imply composition and need, which are impossible for God.
Multiplicity would require parts, contradicting divine simplicity.
3
Learn that creatures cannot share divine attributes
Examine the negation of 'the separate' (al-manfasil): no creature can have attributes like God's—such as independent power, will, or knowledge—because God has no likeness.
This establishes God's uniqueness in His perfect attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحد، ولكن قدرته مع ذلك متعلقة بجميع الممكنات، وعلمه كاشف عن جميع المعلومات، وإرادته مخصصة لجميع الممكنات، وكذا يقال في جميع صفاته، فالتعدد في الصفات محال. وتنفي المنفصل بأن لا يكون لأحد من المخلوقين صفات كصفات الله تعالى، بأن تكون له قدرة توجد وإرادة تخصص وعلم محيط، وغير ذلك، وهذا محال لأن الله لا شبيه له. ووحدانية الأفعال تنفي الكم المنفصل فقط، بأن يكون غيره يفعل كفعله وهذا محال، لأن الله لا شريك له في أفعاله بل هو المنفرد بالإيجاد والإعدام، والمخلوقات ليس لها تأثير إلا قيام الفعل بها نتيجة لاكتسابها له، ويجب أن نعتقد أن الأفعال كلها لله تعالى. دل على وجوب الوحدانية له تعالى الكتاب والسنة والإجماع والعقل، أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى (وَإِلَهُكُمْ إِلَهُ وَاحِدٌ)، والسنة قوله: 'إن الله وتر يحب الوتر'، وأما الإجماع فقد أجمعت الأمة على أن الله واحد. وبرهان العقل فسيأتي.
One, but His power, with that, relates to all possible things, and His knowledge discloses all known things, and His will specifies all possible things, and similarly is said regarding all His attributes, so multiplicity in attributes is impossible. And it negates the separate [attribute] by that there should not be for any of the creatures attributes like the attributes of God Almighty, such that he has a power that brings into existence, a will that specifies, an encompassing knowledge, and other than that, and this is impossible because God has no likeness. And the oneness of actions negates only the separate quantity, such that another does an act like His act, and this is impossible, because God has no partner in His actions, rather He alone brings into existence and annihilates, and creatures have no effect except the occurrence of the action from them as a result of their acquisition of it, and it is necessary to believe that all actions belong to God Almighty. The Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and reason have indicated the necessity of oneness for Him Almighty. As for the Book, His saying Exalted: 'And your God is one God' (al-Baqarah 163); as for the Sunnah, his saying: 'Indeed God is odd and loves oddness'; as for consensus, the community has unanimously agreed that God is one. And the rational proof will come later.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents a multi-part argument for divine oneness (tawhid). First, it addresses the oneness of attributes: although God's power, knowledge, and will are each single, they relate to all possible things without implying multiplicity in the essence. Second, it negates the possibility of creatures having attributes like God's—such as independent power, will, or knowledge—since God has no likeness. Third, it affirms the oneness of actions: no other being can act as God does; only God creates and annihilates, while creatures only 'acquire' actions without producing them. Finally, it cites scriptural proofs: the Qur'anic verse (2:163), the hadith 'God is odd and loves oddness,' and the consensus of the ummah, noting that the rational proof will follow later.

Key Terms

القدرة
العلم
الإرادة

الشبيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because God has many actions, He must have multiple attributes or parts.
Correction: Each attribute is a single perfection relating to all objects, not multiple. Multiplicity would imply composition, which is impossible for God.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi say multiplicity in God's attributes is impossible?
A) Because God's attributes are separate from His essence.
B) Because each attribute, though one in itself, relates to all its objects without division.
C) Because creatures also have similar attributes.
D) Because the Qur'an does not mention multiple attributes.

Key Takeaway
God's oneness means His attributes are single and unique, and no creature resembles Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you desire power, knowledge, or control, do you feel a pang of jealousy toward God’s absolute ownership of these attributes? How does this lesson confront that hidden resentment in your heart? What will you do today to surrender that desire to Him alone?
?
If God has no likeness, what does that demand from your worship? Are you ever tempted to imagine God as having human-like qualities to make Him more relatable? How does this passage push you to purify your concept of God, even if it feels uncomfortable? Write one specific way you will adjust your dhikr or dua to reflect His incomparability.
?
The passage says creatures cannot have attributes like God's. Have you ever secretly wished you had God's power to control outcomes, or His perfect knowledge to avoid mistakes? How does this truth humble you and call you to trust His complete authority? What is one area of your life where you need to stop trying to be 'like God' and instead submit?

Oneness of God’s Actions and Scriptural Proofs
Sanusi affirms oneness of actions and lists scriptural proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that only God brings existence and annihilation, while creatures merely acquire actions, and you will know the scriptural evidence for divine oneness.

Core Idea
God alone creates; creatures only acquire. Scripture affirms His oneness.

Sanusi now turns to the oneness of actions: no other being can act as God does—only He creates and annihilates. Creatures have no independent power; their actions are acquired from God. He then cites the Qur'an, hadith, and consensus to prove that God is one, mentioning that the rational proof will come later.

Guided Path
1
Understand God’s exclusive power over creation
Read the passage that explains God alone brings into existence (ījād) and annihilates (i‘dām). No other being can perform these acts independently.
This negates any partner in actions (shirk fī al-af‘āl).
2
Recognize the nature of human action (acquisition)
Notice the phrase 'creatures have no effect except the occurrence of the action from them as a result of their acquisition (iktisāb) of it.' This means humans are responsible for their actions but they do not create them—God creates both the action and the ability.
Acquisition (kasb) is the Ash‘arī doctrine reconciling human responsibility with divine omnipotence.
3
Learn the scriptural proofs from Quran, hadith, consensus
Identify the three sources cited: Qur'an 2:163, the hadith 'God is odd and loves oddness,' and the consensus of the Muslim community. Notice that the rational proof is promised later.
These proofs establish the necessity of God's oneness from revelation and communal agreement.

Source Text

Introduction to the Divine Impossibilities
Sanusi introduces the twenty impossibilities as opposites of the twenty necessities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why theologians specify twenty impossibilities for God despite the endless possible deficiencies, and how these impossibilities are the direct opposites of the twenty necessary attributes.

Core Idea
The twenty impossibilities are the direct opposites of the twenty necessary attributes.

This passage sets the stage for studying divine attributes by explaining the method: we negate all deficiencies from God, but we focus on twenty specific impossibilities that correspond to the twenty necessities. This approach is both comprehensive and manageable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to get the author's intended meaning.
Note the phrase 'some of what is impossible' – it signals that the list is not exhaustive.
2
Identify the three key claims
Find where the author says: (1) the impossibilities are endless in detail, (2) we must negate all deficiencies generally, and (3) we must know twenty specific impossibilities as opposites of the twenty necessities.
Each claim builds on the previous one.
3
Understand why twenty are singled out
Ask yourself: why only twenty? The answer is that they are the opposites of the twenty necessary attributes. Knowing both sets completes the picture.
This shows the systematic nature of Islamic theology.
4
Relate necessary and impossible attributes
Notice that for every necessary attribute (e.g., existence, eternality), its opposite (non-existence, temporality) is impossible. The two sets are mirrors.
This relationship is fundamental to kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقلنا بعض ما يستحيل لأن المستحيلات على الله لا نهاية لها تفصيلاً، فنفي كل كمال له تعالى نقص، يجب تنزيه الله عنه، وكل ما قدره العقل من نقص يستحيل على الله تعالى، فيجب علينا نفيه على العموم، وإنما يجب علينا معرفة عشرين مستحيلا هي أضداد (۲) العشرين الواجبة ، ويجب أيضاً أن نعرف العشرين الواجبة فكل ما ينافيها فهو مستحيل على الله تعالى.
And we said 'some of what is impossible' because the impossibilities for God have no end in detail. For the negation of every perfection with respect to Him is a deficiency that must be negated from God. And every deficiency that the mind conceives is impossible for God. So we must negate it in general. But we must specifically know twenty impossibilities, which are the opposites of the twenty necessities. And we must also know the twenty necessities, for everything that contradicts them is impossible for God.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage serves as an introduction to the list of divine impossibilities. The author explains that while the specific impossibilities are endless, the theologian is required to know twenty particular ones that directly oppose the twenty necessary attributes. The principle is that any lack of perfection is a deficiency, and every deficiency must be negated from God. Since the necessary attributes are the perfections, their opposites are the impossibilities. This establishes the method of theology: understanding God through pairs of necessary and impossible attributes.

Key Terms
المستحيلات
العشرين الواجبة
أضداد
نفي الكمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that only twenty things are impossible for God.
Correction: The passage explicitly says the impossibilities have no end in detail; we only must know twenty.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say 'some of what is impossible' (بعض ما يستحيل)?
A) Because it is impossible to know them all.
B) Because the impossibilities are endless in detail.
C) Because only twenty are truly impossible.
D) Because the list is incomplete.

Key Takeaway
The twenty impossibilities are opposites of the twenty necessities; together they form a complete description of what must be affirmed and negated about God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's perfection, do you ever limit it to the twenty attributes? What does this passage's emphasis on 'no end in detail' reveal about the limitations of your own understanding? How will you seek to expand your awe of His infinite perfection?
?
Can you recall a moment when you unconsciously attributed a deficiency to God—perhaps by doubting His wisdom in a trial? This passage says every deficiency is impossible for Him. How does this truth confront that doubt, and what will you do the next time such a thought arises?
?
The twenty impossibilities are opposites of the twenty necessities. Which of your own character traits is the opposite of a divine perfection? For example, if God is Eternal, do you live as if you will last forever? What one change will you make today to align your heart with His necessary attributes?

The Impossibility of Nonexistence for Allah
Sanusi defines al-'adam and rules it impossible for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-'adam (nonexistence) and why it is impossible for Allah.

Core Idea
Nonexistence is the opposite of existence and impossible for God.

Sanusi now turns to the specific impossibilities for Allah. The first is nonexistence (al-'adam). He defines it clearly and then applies the logical relationship between necessary and impossible attributes. This short passage establishes a key building block for understanding divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic definition
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice the terms 'al-ʻadam', 'al-wujūd', and 'ḍidd'.
The passage is a single sentence, so read it multiple times.
2
Understand the term 'ḍidd'
The word 'ḍidd' means 'opposite'. Nonexistence is the logical opposite of existence.
In logic, opposites cannot coexist.
3
Connect to necessary existence
Recall that existence (al-wujūd) is necessary (wājib) for Allah. Therefore, its opposite, nonexistence, is impossible (mustaḥīl).
This is a direct application of the rule: necessary and impossible are mutually exclusive.
4
Reflect on the implication
Understand that Allah's existence is not just a fact but a necessity. It is inconceivable for Him not to exist.
This strengthens tawḥīd by negating any possibility of non-existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العدم : وهو ضد الوجود وهو عبارة عن لا شيء فالوجود لله واجب والعدم مستحيل عليه تعالى.
Nonexistence (al-'adam): It is the opposite of existence, and it is expressed as 'nothing'. So existence is necessary for God, and nonexistence is impossible for Him.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage defines the first specific impossibility: nonexistence (al-'adam). It is described as the opposite of existence, meaning no being at all. Since existence (al-wujud) is a necessary attribute of God, the opposite, nonexistence, is necessarily impossible for Him. This is a straightforward application of the relationship between necessary and impossible attributes.

Key Terms
العدم
الوجود
ضد
واجب
مستحيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Nonexistence might be thought of as a mere absence that could be possible for God.
Correction: Nonexistence is defined as the opposite of existence, and since existence is necessary for God, nonexistence is impossible. It is not just an absence but a logical impossibility.

Checkpoint
What is al-'adam defined as in this passage?
A) The absence of perfection.
B) The opposite of existence, expressed as 'nothing'.
C) The opposite of necessity.
D) A deficiency in attributes.

Key Takeaway
Al-'adam is the opposite of existence and rationally impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If nonexistence is impossible for Allah, then your very being at this moment is a direct act of His will. Are you living with the constant awareness that you exist only because He chooses to sustain you, or do you take your existence for granted?
?
When you feel overwhelmed by life’s changes and fears of loss, do you anchor yourself in the certainty that Allah’s existence is absolute and unchanging? How would your daily worries shift if you truly internalised that His nonexistence is impossible?
?
Recognising that al-'adam is opposite to existence and impossible for Allah, what does that say about your own moments of spiritual emptiness? Could they be a call to return to the One whose existence is always present, even when your own feels fragile?

The Impossibility of Origination (al-Huduth) for God
Definition of al-huduth as opposite of pre-eternity and statement of its impossibility for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-huduth, why it is the opposite of pre-eternity, and why it is impossible for God.

Core Idea
Origination means coming into being after nonexistence, impossible for the pre-eternal God.

After establishing that pre-eternity (al-qidam) is necessary for God, Sanusi now defines its opposite: origination (al-huduth). This short but precise passage clarifies what al-huduth means and why it is impossible for God. Understanding this term is essential for grasping the divine attributes of pre-eternity and necessary existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice its concise structure defining a theological term.
The passage is only one sentence in Arabic but contains a complete definition.
2
Identify the definition and opposite
Find where al-huduth is defined as the opposite of pre-eternity. Understand that these two terms are mutually exclusive.
3
Understand the impossibility for God
Why is origination impossible for God? Because pre-eternity is necessary for Him, and a thing cannot be both pre-eternal and originated.
This directly follows from the definition.
4
Grasp the meaning of 'al-hadith'
The passage defines 'al-hadith' as anything that was not and then came to be. This applies to all created things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحدوث : وهو ضد القدم فالقدم واجب الله و الحدوث مستحيل عليه تعالى والمراد بالحدوث هو التجدد بعد العدم فكل من لم يكن ثم كان فهو الحادث (۳) .
Origination (al-huduth): It is the opposite of pre-eternity. So pre-eternity is necessary for God, and origination is impossible for Him. By origination is meant renewal after nonexistence, so everything that was not and then came to be is originated (al-hadith).
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage defines the second specific impossibility: origination (al-huduth). It is the opposite of pre-eternity (al-qidam), which is a necessary attribute of God. The author clarifies that origination means coming into being after a state of nonexistence. Since God is pre-eternal, He never was nonexistent, so origination is impossible for Him. The term 'al-hadith' is defined as that which was not and then came to be.

Key Terms
الحدوث
القدم
ضد
التجدد بعد العدم
الحادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Origination (al-huduth) means change over time.
Correction: In this passage, al-huduth specifically means renewal after nonexistence, not mere change.

Checkpoint
What does al-huduth signify according to this passage?
A) Change over time.
B) Renewal after nonexistence.
C) Temporal limitation.
D) The opposite of necessity.

Key Takeaway
Origination (al-huduth) is the opposite of pre-eternity and means coming into being after nonexistence; it is impossible for God because He is pre-eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage defines origination as 'renewal after nonexistence'. You, like all creation, are originated. In what areas of your life are you living as though you are self-sufficient, forgetting that you were nothing and God brought you into being? What will you do today to consciously acknowledge your dependence on Him?
?
If origination is impossible for God because He is pre-eternal, how does this truth affect the way you view your own temporariness? Does the fleeting nature of your existence make you cling more tightly to the Eternal One, or do you still act as if this world is permanent? Name one specific attachment you need to loosen because of this reality.
?
The text says 'everything that was not and then came to be is originated.' When you look at your possessions, relationships, and even your own life, they all share this quality. Are you valuing temporary things as if they were eternal? What would it look like to treat every 'originated' thing as a gift from the Pre-Eternal God, rather than an end in itself?

God's Self-Subsistence and Refutation of Incarnation
Proves God's self-subsistence and refutes incarnation by showing it reduces God to an attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must be self-subsistent and why incarnation (hulul) is impossible, based on the argument that it would reduce Him to an attribute.

Core Idea
If God indwells in anything, He becomes an attribute—but He is the possessor of attributes.

In this passage, Sanusi continues his proof of God's attributes by establishing that God is self-subsistent (qa'im bi-nafsihi). He then refutes two groups who claim God indwells in a created being: Christians who say God dwelt in Jesus, and the Batiniyya who say God indwells in perfect saints. The argument is tight: indwelling would make God an attribute, but God is described with essential and relational attributes, which an attribute cannot possess. This lesson unpacks that proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Let the author's own structure come through.
Notice how the passage moves from a general impossibility to a specific refutation.
2
Identify the two false doctrines
The passage refutes two groups: Christians who claim God dwelt in Jesus, and the Batiniyya who claim God indwells in perfect saints. Mark these in the text.
Both are considered kufr (disbelief) by the author.
3
Follow the logical argument
Trace the argument: if God indwells in something, He becomes an attribute of it. But God is described with attributes of meaning and relational attributes. An attribute cannot be described with attributes because a meaning cannot subsist in a meaning. Therefore, incarnation is impossible.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
4
Reflect on divine transcendence
Consider how this argument preserves God's uniqueness: He is a self (dhat) unlike any other, and His attributes are unlike any others.
This is a cornerstone of Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحيل عليه أن لا يكون قائماً بنفسه : بأن يكون صفة حادثة أو قديمة تقوم بمحل، أو تحتاج إلى مخصص فيستحيل على الله تعالى أن يحل بذات كما تحل الصفة في موصوفها كما تدعيه النصارى والباطنية المنحرفون عن الصراط، فالنصارى قالوا حل الإله بذات عيسى والباطنية طائفة منحرفة قالوا : الولي الكامل يحل الله فيه، وهذا کله کفر صريح، لأن الله لو حل في شيء لكان صفة له ولو كان صفة له لم يصح وصفه بصفات المعاني والمعنوية لأن المعنى لا يقوم بمعنى ومولانا جل وعز يجب اتصافه بهما، فليس بصفة بل هو ذات لا تشبه الذوات، وصفاته لا تشبه الصفات
And it is impossible for Him not to be self-subsistent: that is, that He should be a contingent or eternal attribute subsisting in a subject, or need a specifier. So it is impossible for Allah to indwell in a self like the way attributes indwell in their subjects, as the Christians and the Batiniyya deviants claim. The Christians said that the deity indwelt in the self of Jesus, and the Batiniyya are a deviant sect who said that the perfect saint is indwelt by Allah. All this is clear disbelief, because if Allah were to indwell in something, He would be an attribute of it; and if He were an attribute of it, He would not be described with the attributes of meaning and relational attributes, because a meaning does not subsist in a meaning. And our Lord, exalted and glorified, must be described with both, so He is not an attribute but is a self that does not resemble selves, and His attributes do not resemble attributes.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God is self-subsistent (قائم بنفسه) and not an attribute subsisting in a subject. The author argues that if God were not self-subsistent, He would be an attribute needing a subject or a specifier. He then refutes the doctrines of incarnation (حلول) held by Christians (who say God dwelt in Jesus) and the Batiniyya (who say God indwells in perfect saints). The argument: if God indwells in something, He becomes an attribute of that thing. But God is described with attributes of meaning (صفات المعاني, like knowledge) and relational attributes (صفات معنوية, like willing). An attribute cannot subsist in another attribute. Therefore, God cannot be an attribute; He is a unique self (ذات) unlike all selves, and His attributes are unlike all attributes.

Key Terms
قائماً بنفسه
صفة
حلول
النصارى
الباطنية
صفات المعاني
الصفات المعنوية
ذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God can indwell in a saint because He is powerful.
Correction: If God indwells, He becomes an attribute; but attributes cannot possess other attributes. Since God possesses attributes, He cannot be an attribute.

Checkpoint
Why is incarnation (hulul) impossible according to the passage?
A) Because God is too great to dwell in a small body.
B) Because if God dwells in something, He would become an attribute of that thing, which contradicts His being a self-subsistent essence possessing attributes.
C) Because Jesus denied it.
D) Because the saints are pure and cannot be indwelt.

Key Takeaway
God cannot indwell in anything because that would reduce Him to an attribute, contradicting His nature as a self-subsistent essence that possesses attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What specific assumptions in your own heart about God's nearness or intervention in your life might actually be a subtle form of expecting Him to 'indwell' in a created thing (your feelings, a person, a place)? How does this lesson call you to repent of such thinking and instead seek Him through His described attributes?
?
When you feel spiritually distant, do you secretly desire an immediate, tangible union with God that bypasses the means He has prescribed? How does the truth that God cannot indwell anything free you from false hopes and push you to pursue closeness through obedience and knowledge of His names?
?
The Batiniyya claimed that perfect saints become vessels for God. Is there any person or object in your life that you treat as if it contains a special divine presence, even subtly? How does this lesson demand you reassess that attachment and return to the understanding that God alone is self-subsistent and transcendent?

The Logical Proof Against Union
Provides a logical proof of the impossibility of union.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that makes the union of two things impossible, and why this refutes any doctrine that claims union between God and creation.

Core Idea
Union of two things is impossible under all logical possibilities.

After warning against the doctrines of incarnation and union, the author provides a crisp logical proof. By examining the three possible outcomes of two things uniting, we see that each case either leaves them as two or produces something else entirely. This proof is the backbone of the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Read the Arabic note and its translation carefully. The author states that union is absolutely impossible and then gives three scenarios.
The proof is concise but covers all logical possibilities.
2
Analyze the three scenarios
Identify each scenario: both remain, both cease, or one ceases. For each, understand why union does not occur.
The proof is a classic example of disjunctive syllogism.
3
Connect to the overall doctrine
Relate this proof to the refutation of union (ittihad). How does this logical impossibility show the falsity of any belief that God and creation become one?
The proof applies to any two things, eternal or created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثل الحلول في الاستحالة الاتحاد، وهو صيرورة الشيئين شيئاً واحداً وكذلك الباطنية قالوا في الولي، قال في الإضاءة : عليه استعارة، فظهر الفرق بينهما فإن ما نحن فيه العبادة مطلوبة ادعاء وتنزيلاً سواء ترتب على الخلق أو لا، وفي الآية المذكورة ترتب العداوة على الالتقاط بالفعل مع عدم كونه مطلوبا فاللام فيهما استعارة وإن تغاير جهة الاستعارة فيهما وقس على ذلك ما عداهما. ولا تصخ لمذهب النصارى أو من إلى دعوى حلول صارا وذاك كالقول بالاتحاد نحلة أهل الزيغ والإلحاد وموهم المحذور من كلام قوم من الصوفية الأعلام جرياً على عرفهم المخصوص يرجع بالتأويل للنصوص والحاصل أن القول بالحلول والاتحاد كفر ، بل الجهل بأنه كفر كفر. ملاحظة : صيرورة الشيئين شيئاً واحداً مستحيل مطلقاً في القديم والحادث. وبرهانه أن الشيئين إذا اتحدا فإن بقيا موجودين على حالهما فلا اتحاد لأنهما إثنان، وإن عُدما معاً كان الموجود غيرهما فلم يتحدا ، وإن عدم أحدهما دون الآخر، امتنع الاتحاد لأن المعدوم ليس عين الموجود والقول بالاتحاد كفر بإجماع المسلمين.
And analogous to incarnation in impossibility is union, which is the transformation of two things into one thing. And likewise the Batiniyya said concerning the saint. He said in al-Ida'a: it is a metaphor; so the difference between them appears, for what we are dealing with is that worship is sought by claim and representation whether it follows from creation or not, whereas in the mentioned verse the enmity follows from the act of picking up even though it is not sought, so the lam in both is a metaphor even if the direction of metaphor differs in them; and analogize to that what is other than them. And do not listen to the doctrine of the Christians or those who claim incarnation, for that has become like the saying of union, the cult of the people of deviation and atheism; and the seemingly problematic [statements] from some of the eminent Sufis, following their particular convention, are to be interpreted according to texts. And the conclusion is that the saying of incarnation and union is disbelief; indeed, ignorance that it is disbelief is disbelief. Note: The transformation of two things into one thing is absolutely impossible in the eternal and the created. Its proof: that if two things unite, then if they remain existing as they are, there is no union because they are two; if they both cease to exist, then what exists is something else, so they have not united; if one ceases to exist and not the other, union is impossible because the non-existent is not the same as the existent. And the saying of union is disbelief by consensus of the Muslims.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage refutes the doctrine of union (اتحاد) between God and creation. The author begins by stating that union is as impossible as incarnation (حلول). He then quotes from the work 'al-Ida'a' to explain a metaphorical use of language in a previous verse (likely about worship and enmity). This digression clarifies that certain words are metaphorical. He then warns against the doctrines of incarnation and union, calling them the cult of deviation and atheism. He notes that any ambiguous statements from eminent Sufis that might suggest union must be interpreted figuratively. The conclusion is that believing in incarnation or union is disbelief, and even ignorance of this fact is disbelief. The core proof is given in the note: union of two things into one is impossible because if both remain, they are still two; if both vanish, a third thing emerges; if one vanishes, the remaining is not the same as the vanished. Thus union is impossible in all scenarios, and by consensus of Muslims, it is disbelief.

Key Terms
الاتحاد
صيرورة الشيئين شيئاً واحداً
مستحيل
برهان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the three possibilities examined in the proof against union?
A) Both are one from the beginning, both are separate, or one becomes the other.
B) Both remain, both vanish, or one vanishes.
C) Both are material, both are spiritual, or one is material and one spiritual.
D) Both are eternal, both are temporal, or one eternal and one temporal.

Key Takeaway
The logical proof shows that union of two things is impossible in every scenario, and belief in union is therefore disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you desire something forbidden, do you try to convince yourself that you can love both Allah and that desire without conflict? This lesson proves that two cannot become one—will you continue trying to unite them, or will you choose one?
